<p><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/70px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="70" height="70" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/105px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/140px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2424" data-file-height="2425" />
</p>
<a href="/wiki/List_of_personal_coats_of_arms_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of personal coats of arms of Presidents of the United States"><img alt="Coat of Arms of Franklin Roosevelt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Coat_of_Arms_of_Franklin_Roosevelt.svg/40px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Franklin_Roosevelt.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Coat_of_Arms_of_Franklin_Roosevelt.svg/60px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Franklin_Roosevelt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Coat_of_Arms_of_Franklin_Roosevelt.svg/80px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Franklin_Roosevelt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="395" data-file-height="552" /></a></td>
</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;text-align:center;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_series" title="Template:Franklin D. Roosevelt series"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_series" title="Template talk:Franklin D. Roosevelt series"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_series&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Franklin Delano Roosevelt</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/əl/: &#39;le&#39; in &#39;bottle&#39;">əl</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-AHD_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AHD-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> January 30, 1882 – April 12, 1945), often referred to by the initials <b>FDR</b>, was an American statesman and political leader who served as the 32nd <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president of the United States</a> from 1933 until his death in 1945. A member of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>, he won a record four <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">presidential elections</a> and became a central figure in world events during the first half of the 20th century. Roosevelt directed the federal government during most of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, implementing his <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> domestic agenda in response to the worst economic crisis in U.S. history. As a dominant leader of his party, he built the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="New Deal Coalition">New Deal Coalition</a>, which realigned American politics into the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Party_System" title="Fifth Party System">Fifth Party System</a> and defined <a href="/wiki/Modern_American_liberalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern American liberalism">American liberalism</a> throughout the middle third of the 20th century. His third and fourth terms were dominated by <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, which ended shortly after he died in office. He is <a href="/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States" title="Historical rankings of presidents of the United States">rated by scholars</a> as one of the three greatest U.S. presidents, along with <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>, but has also been subject to <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Criticism of Franklin D. Roosevelt">substantial criticism</a>.
</p><p>Roosevelt was born in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_New_York" title="Hyde Park, New York">Hyde Park, New York</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_family" title="Roosevelt family">Dutch American family</a> made well known by the reputation of <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a>, the 26th president of the United States, and <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Aspinwall" title="William Henry Aspinwall">William Henry Aspinwall</a>. FDR attended <a href="/wiki/Groton_School" title="Groton School">Groton School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_College" title="Harvard College">Harvard College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Law_School" title="Columbia Law School">Columbia Law School</a>, and went on to practice law in New York City. In 1905, he married his fifth cousin once removed, <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>. They had six children, of whom five survived into adulthood. He won election to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Senate" title="New York State Senate">New York State Senate</a> in 1910, and then served as <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Assistant Secretary of the Navy">Assistant Secretary of the Navy</a> under President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Roosevelt was <a href="/wiki/James_M._Cox" title="James M. Cox">James M. Cox</a>'s running mate on the Democratic Party's <a href="/wiki/1920_United_States_presidential_election" title="1920 United States presidential election">1920</a> national ticket, but Cox was defeated by Republican Warren G. Harding. In 1921, Roosevelt contracted a <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt%27s_paralytic_illness" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt&#39;s paralytic illness">paralytic illness</a>, believed at the time to be <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a>, and his legs became permanently paralyzed. While attempting to recover from his condition, Roosevelt founded the <a href="/wiki/Warm_Springs_Historic_District" title="Warm Springs Historic District">treatment center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warm_Springs,_Georgia" title="Warm Springs, Georgia">Warm Springs, Georgia</a>, for people with <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" class="mw-redirect" title="Poliomyelitis">poliomyelitis</a>. In spite of being unable to walk unaided, Roosevelt returned to public office by winning election as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_York" title="Governor of New York">Governor of New York</a> in 1928. He was in office from 1929 to 1933 and served as a reform Governor, promoting programs to combat the economic crisis besetting the United States at the time.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1932_United_States_presidential_election" title="1932 United States presidential election">1932 presidential election</a>, Roosevelt defeated <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> President <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a> in a landslide. Roosevelt took office in the midst of <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States" title="Great Depression in the United States">the Great Depression</a>, the worst economic crisis in United States History. During the <a href="/wiki/First_100_days_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt%27s_presidency" title="First 100 days of Franklin D. Roosevelt&#39;s presidency">first 100 days</a> of the <a href="/wiki/73rd_United_States_Congress" title="73rd United States Congress">73rd United States Congress</a>, Roosevelt spearheaded unprecedented federal legislation and issued a profusion of executive orders that instituted the New Deal—a variety of programs designed to produce relief, recovery, and reform. He created numerous programs to provide relief to the unemployed and farmers while seeking economic recovery with the <a href="/wiki/National_Recovery_Administration" title="National Recovery Administration">National Recovery Administration</a> and other programs. He also instituted major regulatory reforms related to finance, communications, and labor, and presided over the end of <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">Prohibition</a>. He harnessed radio to speak directly to the American people, giving 30 "<a href="/wiki/Fireside_chat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fireside chat">fireside chat</a>" radio addresses during his presidency and becoming the first American president to be televised. The economy having improved rapidly from 1933 to 1936, Roosevelt won a landslide <a href="/wiki/1936_United_States_presidential_election" title="1936 United States presidential election">reelection in 1936</a>. However, the economy then relapsed into a deep recession in 1937 and 1938. After the 1936 election, Roosevelt sought passage of the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_Reorganization_Bill_of_1937" class="mw-redirect" title="Judiciary Reorganization Bill of 1937">Judiciary Reorganization Bill of 1937</a> (the "court packing plan"), which would have expanded the size of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a>. The bipartisan <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative Coalition">Conservative Coalition</a> that formed in 1937 prevented passage of the bill and blocked the implementation of further New Deal programs and reforms. Major surviving programs and legislation implemented under Roosevelt include the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Act_of_1935" title="National Labor Relations Act of 1935">National Labor Relations Act</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Labor_Standards_Act_of_1938" title="Fair Labor Standards Act of 1938">Fair Labor Standards Act of 1938</a>, which, among other things, prohibited child labor and created the right to a minimum wage.
</p><p>The United States reelected FDR in <a href="/wiki/1940_United_States_presidential_election" title="1940 United States presidential election">1940</a> for his third term, making him the only U.S. President to serve for more than two terms. With World War II looming after 1938, Roosevelt gave strong diplomatic and financial support to <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and eventually the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> while the U.S. remained officially neutral. Following the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> on December 7, 1941, an event he famously called "<a href="/wiki/Infamy_Speech" title="Infamy Speech">a date which will live in infamy</a>", Roosevelt obtained a congressional declaration of war on Japan, and, a few days later, on <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a>. Assisted by his top aide <a href="/wiki/Harry_Hopkins" title="Harry Hopkins">Harry Hopkins</a> and with very strong national support, he worked closely with British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> and Chinese <a href="/wiki/Generalissimo" title="Generalissimo">Generalissimo</a> <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> in leading the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Powers_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Allied Powers (World War II)">Allied Powers</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a>. Roosevelt supervised the mobilization of the U.S. economy to support the war effort, and implemented a <a href="/wiki/Europe_first" title="Europe first">Europe first</a> strategy, making the defeat of Germany a priority over that of Japan. He also initiated the development of the world's first <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear bomb">atomic bomb</a>, and worked with the other Allied leaders to lay the groundwork for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and other post-war institutions. Roosevelt won reelection in <a href="/wiki/1944_United_States_presidential_election" title="1944 United States presidential election">1944</a>, but with his physical health declining during the war years, he died in April 1945, just 11 weeks into his fourth term. The Axis Powers surrendered to the Allies in the months following Roosevelt's death, during the presidency of his successor, <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a>.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Third_and_fourth_terms_(1941–1945)"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Third and fourth terms (1941–1945)</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23"><a href="#Lead-up_to_the_war"><span class="tocnumber">6.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Lead-up to the war</span></a></li>

<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-26"><a href="#Nuclear_program"><span class="tocnumber">6.3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Nuclear program</span></a></li>

</ul>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_marriage">Early life and marriage</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood">Childhood</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg/220px-Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="282" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg/330px-Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg/440px-Franklin-Roosevelt-1884.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="768" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">A young, <a href="/wiki/Breeching_(boys)" title="Breeching (boys)">unbreeched</a> Roosevelt in 1884, 2 years old<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg/220px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="340" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg/330px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg/440px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_portrait_-_NARA_-_196689.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1896" data-file-height="2929" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Roosevelt in 1893, at the age of 11</div></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_D._Roosevelt,_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton,_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Franklin_D._Roosevelt%2C_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton%2C_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg/220px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt%2C_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton%2C_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="341" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Franklin_D._Roosevelt%2C_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton%2C_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg/330px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt%2C_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton%2C_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Franklin_D._Roosevelt%2C_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton%2C_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg/440px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt%2C_a_formal_portrait_in_Groton%2C_Massachusetts_-_NARA_-_196688.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1865" data-file-height="2888" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Roosevelt in 1900, at the age of 18</div></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Franklin Delano Roosevelt was born on January 30, 1882, in the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Valley" title="Hudson Valley">Hudson Valley</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_New_York" title="Hyde Park, New York">Hyde Park, New York</a>, to businessman <a href="/wiki/James_Roosevelt_I" title="James Roosevelt I">James Roosevelt I</a> and his second wife, <a href="/wiki/Sara_Ann_Delano" class="mw-redirect" title="Sara Ann Delano">Sara Ann Delano</a>. Roosevelt's parents, who were sixth cousins,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns19567_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns19567-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> both came from wealthy old New York families, the <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_family" title="Roosevelt family">Roosevelts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Aspinwall" title="William Henry Aspinwall">Aspinwalls</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Delano_family" title="Delano family">Delanos</a>, respectively. Roosevelt's patrilineal ancestor migrated to <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> in the 17th century, and the Roosevelts flourished as merchants and landowners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201718_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201718-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The Delano family progenitor traveled to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Mayflower" title="Mayflower">Mayflower</a></i>, and the Delanos prospered as merchants and shipbuilders in <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201719_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201719-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Franklin had a half-brother, <a href="/wiki/James_Roosevelt_Roosevelt" title="James Roosevelt Roosevelt">James "Rosy" Roosevelt</a>, from his father's previous marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith20075–6_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith20075–6-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt grew up in a wealthy family. His father, James Roosevelt I, graduated from <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Law_School" title="Harvard Law School">Harvard Law School</a> in 1851, but chose not to practice law after receiving an inheritance from his grandfather, <a href="/wiki/James_Roosevelt_(1760%E2%80%931847)" title="James Roosevelt (1760–1847)">James Roosevelt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith20075–6_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith20075–6-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt's father was a prominent <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Democrat" title="Bourbon Democrat">Bourbon Democrat</a> who once took Franklin to meet President <a href="/wiki/Grover_Cleveland" title="Grover Cleveland">Grover Cleveland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200771_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200771-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Sara was the dominant influence in Franklin's early years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELash1971111_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELash1971111-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> She once declared, "My son Franklin is a Delano, not a Roosevelt at all."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns19567_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns19567-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> James, who was 54 when Franklin was born, was considered by some as a remote father, though biographer <a href="/wiki/James_MacGregor_Burns" title="James MacGregor Burns">James MacGregor Burns</a> indicates James interacted with his son more than was typical at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns19564_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns19564-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt learned to ride, shoot, row, and to play polo and lawn tennis. He took up golf in his teen years, becoming a skilled long hitter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007110_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007110-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He was club champion in his late teen years at the small golf club on <a href="/wiki/Campobello_Island" title="Campobello Island">Campobello Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, where his family had a summer cottage.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He learned to sail early, and when he was 16, his father gave him a sailboat.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack200521_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack200521-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_early_career">Education and early career</span></h3>
<p>Frequent trips to Europe—he made his first excursion at the age of two and went with his parents every year from the ages of seven to fifteen—helped Roosevelt become <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States_by_languages_spoken" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the United States by languages spoken">conversant</a> in German and French. Except for attending public school in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> at age nine,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200720-25_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200720-25-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950169_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950169-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt was home-schooled by tutors until age 14.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2019)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> He then attended <a href="/wiki/Groton_School" title="Groton School">Groton School</a>, an Episcopal boarding school in <a href="/wiki/Groton,_Massachusetts" title="Groton, Massachusetts">Groton, Massachusetts</a>, joining the third form.<sup id="cite_ref-Brands,_2008_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brands,_2008-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2019)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Its headmaster, <a href="/wiki/Endicott_Peabody_(educator)" title="Endicott Peabody (educator)">Endicott Peabody</a>, preached the duty of Christians to help the less fortunate and urged his students to enter public service. Peabody remained a strong influence throughout Roosevelt's life, officiating at his wedding and visiting him as president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195616_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195616-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950174_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950174-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Like most of his Groton classmates, Roosevelt went to <a href="/wiki/Harvard_College" title="Harvard College">Harvard College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950172_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950172-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt was an average student academically,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200730_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200730-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and he later declared, "I took economics courses in college for four years, and everything I was taught was wrong."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195618,_20_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195618,_20-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a> fraternity<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Fly_Club" title="Fly Club">Fly Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950176_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950176-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt was relatively undistinguished as a student or athlete, but he became editor-in-chief of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Harvard_Crimson" title="The Harvard Crimson">The Harvard Crimson</a></i> daily newspaper, a position that required great ambition, energy, and the ability to manage others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950175_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950175-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt's father died in 1900, causing great distress for him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201728–29_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201728–29-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The following year, Roosevelt's fifth cousin <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> became President of the United States. Theodore's vigorous leadership style and reforming zeal made him Franklin's role model and hero.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195624_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195624-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt graduated from Harvard in 1903 with an <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">A.B.</a> in history. He entered <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Law_School" title="Columbia Law School">Columbia Law School</a> in 1904, but dropped out in 1907 after passing the New York State bar exam.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195628_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195628-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> In 1908, he took a job with the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> firm of <a href="/wiki/Carter_Ledyard_%26_Milburn" title="Carter Ledyard &amp; Milburn">Carter Ledyard &amp; Milburn</a>, working in the firm's <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_law" title="Admiralty law">admiralty law</a> division.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201738–39_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201738–39-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Marriage.2C_family.2C_and_affairs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage,_family,_and_affairs">Marriage, family, and affairs</span></h3>
<p>In mid-1902, Franklin began courting his future wife <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a>, with whom he had been acquainted as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERowley20103–6_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowley20103–6-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Eleanor and Franklin were fifth cousins, once removed,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and Eleanor was a niece of Theodore Roosevelt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERowley20103_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowley20103-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> They began corresponding with each other in 1902, and in October 1903,<sup id="cite_ref-Brands,_2008_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brands,_2008-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (July 2019)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Franklin proposed marriage to Eleanor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200737,_46–47_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200737,_46–47-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 17, 1905, Roosevelt married Eleanor in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, despite the fierce resistance of his mother.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195626_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195626-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> While she did not dislike Eleanor, Sara Roosevelt was very possessive of her son, believing he was too young for marriage. She attempted to break the engagement several times.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950181–83_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950181–83-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Eleanor's uncle, President Theodore Roosevelt, stood in at the wedding for Eleanor's deceased father, <a href="/wiki/Elliott_B._Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Elliott B. Roosevelt">Elliott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201735–36_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201735–36-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The young couple moved into <a href="/wiki/Home_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt_National_Historic_Site" title="Home of Franklin D. Roosevelt National Historic Site">Springwood</a>, his family's estate at Hyde Park. The home was owned by Sara Roosevelt until her death in 1941 and was very much her home as well.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrands2009160_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrands2009160-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Franklin and Sara Roosevelt did the planning and furnishing of a town house Sara had built for the young couple in New York City; Sara had a twin house built alongside for herself. Eleanor never felt at home in the houses at Hyde Park or New York, but she loved the family's vacation home on <a href="/wiki/Campobello_Island" title="Campobello Island">Campobello Island</a>, which Sara gave to the couple.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200754–55_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200754–55-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James,_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park,_New_York_1908.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James%2C_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park%2C_New_York_1908.jpg/220px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James%2C_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park%2C_New_York_1908.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James%2C_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park%2C_New_York_1908.jpg/330px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James%2C_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park%2C_New_York_1908.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James%2C_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park%2C_New_York_1908.jpg/440px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James%2C_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park%2C_New_York_1908.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2714" data-file-height="2790" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_Eleanor_Roosevelt_with_Anna_and_baby_James,_formal_portrait_in_Hyde_Park,_New_York_1908.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eleanor and Franklin with their first two children, 1908</div></div></div>
<p>Biographer James MacGregor Burns said that young Roosevelt was self-assured and at ease in the upper class.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195677–79_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195677–79-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, Eleanor at the time was shy and disliked social life, and at first stayed at home to raise their several children. Like his father had, Franklin left the raising of the children to his wife, while Eleanor in turn largely relied on hired caregivers to raise the children. Referring to her early experience as a mother, she later stated that she knew "absolutely nothing about handling or feeding a baby."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200757–58_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200757–58-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Although Eleanor had an aversion to sexual intercourse and considered it "an ordeal to be endured",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinkler200619–20_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinkler200619–20-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> she and Franklin had six children. <a href="/wiki/Anna_Roosevelt_Halsted" title="Anna Roosevelt Halsted">Anna</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Roosevelt" title="James Roosevelt">James</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Roosevelt" title="Elliott Roosevelt">Elliott</a> were born in 1906, 1907, and 1910, respectively. The couple's second son, Franklin, died in infancy in 1909. Another son, also named <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt_Jr." title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt Jr.">Franklin</a>, was born in 1914, and the youngest child, <a href="/wiki/John_Aspinwall_Roosevelt" title="John Aspinwall Roosevelt">John</a>, was born in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt had various extra-marital affairs, including one with Eleanor's social secretary <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Mercer_Rutherfurd" title="Lucy Mercer Rutherfurd">Lucy Mercer</a>, which began soon after she was hired in early 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007153_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007153-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In September 1918, Eleanor found letters revealing the affair in Roosevelt's luggage. Franklin contemplated divorcing Eleanor, but Sara objected strongly and Lucy would not agree to marry a divorced man with five children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007160_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007160-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Franklin and Eleanor remained married, and Roosevelt promised never to see Lucy again. Eleanor never truly forgave him, and their marriage from that point on was more of a political partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinkler200628,_38,_48–49_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinkler200628,_38,_48–49-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Eleanor soon thereafter established a separate home in Hyde Park at <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt_National_Historic_Site" title="Eleanor Roosevelt National Historic Site">Val-Kill</a>, and increasingly devoted herself to various social and political causes independently of her husband. The emotional break in their marriage was so severe that when Roosevelt asked Eleanor in 1942—in light of his failing health—to come back home and live with him again, she refused.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinkler2006202–03_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinkler2006202–03-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> He was not always aware of when she visited the White House and for some time she could not easily reach him on the telephone without his secretary's help; Roosevelt, in turn, did not visit Eleanor's New York City apartment until late 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950195_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950195-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Franklin broke his promise to Eleanor to refrain from having affairs. He and Lucy maintained a formal correspondence, and began seeing each other again in 1941, or perhaps earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Lucy was with Roosevelt on the day he died in 1945. Despite this, Roosevelt's affair was not widely known until the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinkler2006202–03_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinkler2006202–03-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt's son Elliott claimed that his father had a 20-year affair with his private secretary, <a href="/wiki/Marguerite_LeHand" title="Marguerite LeHand">Marguerite "Missy" LeHand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETully2005340_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETully2005340-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Another son, James, stated that "there is a real possibility that a romantic relationship existed" between his father and <a href="/wiki/Princess_M%C3%A4rtha_of_Sweden" title="Princess Märtha of Sweden">Crown Princess Märtha of Norway</a>, who resided in the White House during part of World War II. Aides began to refer to her at the time as "the president's girlfriend",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin1995153_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin1995153-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and gossip linking the two romantically appeared in the newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERowley2010254_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowley2010254-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Early_political_career_.281910.E2.80.931920.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_political_career_(1910–1920)">Early political career (1910–1920)</span></h2>
<h3><span id="State_senator_.281910.E2.80.931913.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="State_senator_(1910–1913)">State senator (1910–1913)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Woodrow_Wilson,_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Woodrow_Wilson%2C_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg/170px-Woodrow_Wilson%2C_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Woodrow_Wilson%2C_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg/255px-Woodrow_Wilson%2C_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Woodrow_Wilson%2C_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg/340px-Woodrow_Wilson%2C_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Woodrow_Wilson,_New_Jersey_Governor_-_1911.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roosevelt supported Governor <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1912_United_States_presidential_election" title="1912 United States presidential election">1912 presidential election</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg/170px-Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg/255px-Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="281" data-file-height="405" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Theodore_Roosevelt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> was Franklin Roosevelt's distant cousin and an important influence on his career.</div></div></div>
<p>Roosevelt held little passion for the practice of law and confided to friends that he planned to eventually enter politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200758–60_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200758–60-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Despite his admiration for his cousin, Theodore, Franklin inherited his father's affiliation with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201741_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201741-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the <a href="/wiki/1910_New_York_state_election" title="1910 New York state election">1910 elections</a>, the local Democratic Party recruited Roosevelt to run for a seat in the <a href="/wiki/New_York_State_Assembly" title="New York State Assembly">New York State Assembly</a>. Roosevelt was an attractive recruit for the party because Theodore Roosevelt was still one of the country's most prominent politicians, and a Democratic Roosevelt was good publicity; the candidate could also pay for his own campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200760–62_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200760–62-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt's campaign for the state assembly ended after the Democratic incumbent, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Stuyvesant_Chanler" title="Lewis Stuyvesant Chanler">Lewis Stuyvesant Chanler</a>, chose to seek re-election. Rather than putting his political hopes on hold, Roosevelt ran for a seat in the state senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200760–64_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200760–64-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The senate district, located in <a href="/wiki/Dutchess_County,_New_York" title="Dutchess County, New York">Dutchess County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_County,_New_York" title="Columbia County, New York">Columbia County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Putnam_County,_New_York" title="Putnam County, New York">Putnam County</a>, was strongly <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200765_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200765-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt feared that open opposition from Theodore could effectively end his campaign, but Theodore privately encouraged his cousin's candidacy despite their differences in partisan affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201741_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201741-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Acting as his own campaign manager, Roosevelt traveled throughout the senate district via <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobile</a> at a time when many could not afford cars.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200765–66_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200765–66-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Due to his aggressive and effective campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950202–03_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950202–03-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> the Roosevelt name's influence in the Hudson Valley, and the Democratic landslide <a href="/wiki/United_States_elections,_1910" class="mw-redirect" title="United States elections, 1910">that year</a>, Roosevelt won the election, surprising almost everyone.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195634_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195634-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Though legislative sessions rarely lasted more than ten weeks, Roosevelt treated his new position as a full-time career.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200768–69_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200768–69-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Taking his seat on January 1, 1911, Roosevelt immediately became the leader of a group of "Insurgents" who opposed the <a href="/wiki/Bossism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bossism">bossism</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Tammany_Hall" title="Tammany Hall">Tammany Hall</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_machine" title="Political machine">machine</a> that dominated the state Democratic Party. In the <a href="/wiki/1911_United_States_Senate_election_in_New_York" title="1911 United States Senate election in New York">1911 U.S. Senate election</a>, which was determined in a joint session of the New York state legislature,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt and nineteen other Democrats caused a prolonged deadlock by opposing a series of Tammany-backed candidates. Finally, Tammany threw its backing behind <a href="/wiki/James_A._O%27Gorman" class="mw-redirect" title="James A. O&#39;Gorman">James A. O'Gorman</a>, a highly regarded judge who Roosevelt found acceptable, and O'Gorman won the election in late March.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrands200957–60_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrands200957–60-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt soon became a popular figure among New York Democrats, though he had not yet become an eloquent speaker.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195634_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195634-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> News articles and cartoons began depicting "the second coming of a Roosevelt" that sent "cold shivers down the spine of Tammany".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950205–206_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950205–206-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt, again in opposition to Tammany Hall, supported New Jersey Governor <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>'s successful bid for the <a href="/wiki/1912_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1912 Democratic National Convention">1912 Democratic nomination</a>, earning an informal designation as an original Wilson man.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195649_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195649-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The election became a three-way contest, as Theodore Roosevelt left the Republican Party to launch a <a href="/wiki/Third_party_(United_States)" title="Third party (United States)">third party</a> campaign against Wilson and sitting Republican President <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a>. Franklin's decision to back Wilson over Theodore Roosevelt in the <a href="/wiki/1912_United_States_presidential_election" title="1912 United States presidential election">general election</a> alienated some members of his family, although Theodore himself was not offended.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack200562–63_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack200562–63-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Wilson's victory over the divided Republican Party made him the first Democrat to win a presidential election since 1892. Overcoming a bout with <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a>, and with extensive assistance from journalist <a href="/wiki/Louis_McHenry_Howe" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis McHenry Howe">Louis McHenry Howe</a>, Roosevelt was re-elected in the <a href="/wiki/1912_New_York_state_election" title="1912 New York state election">1912 elections</a>. After the election, he served for a short time as chairman of the Agriculture Committee, and his success with farm and labor bills was a precursor to his New Deal policies twenty years later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195644–46_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195644–46-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> By this time he had become more consistently <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Era" title="Progressive Era">progressive</a>, in support of labor and social welfare programs for women and children; cousin Theodore was of some influence on these issues.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195643_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195643-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy_.281913.E2.80.931919.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy_(1913–1919)">Assistant Secretary of the Navy (1913–1919)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg/220px-Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="319" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg/330px-Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg/440px-Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg 2x" data-file-width="944" data-file-height="1370" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_Roosevelt_Secretary_of_the_Navy_1913.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roosevelt as Assistant Secretary of the Navy, 1913</div></div></div>
<p>Roosevelt's support of Wilson led to his appointment in March 1913 as <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="Assistant Secretary of the Navy">Assistant Secretary of the Navy</a>, the second-ranking official in the Navy Department after Secretary <a href="/wiki/Josephus_Daniels" title="Josephus Daniels">Josephus Daniels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith200797–101_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200797–101-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt had a lifelong affection for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Navy</a>—he had already collected almost 10,000 naval books and claimed to have read all but one—and was more ardent than Daniels in supporting a large and efficient naval force.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195651_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195651-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950209_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950209-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> With Wilson's support, Daniels and Roosevelt instituted a merit-based promotion system and made other reforms to extend civilian control over the autonomous departments of the Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007102–106_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007102–106-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt oversaw the Navy's civilian employees and earned the respect of union leaders for his fairness in resolving disputes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007113–114_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007113–114-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Not a single strike occurred during his seven-plus years in the office,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195652_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195652-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> during which Roosevelt gained experience in labor issues, government management during wartime, naval issues, and logistics, all valuable areas for future office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950212_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950212-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1914, Roosevelt made an ill-conceived decision to run for the seat of retiring Republican Senator <a href="/wiki/Elihu_Root" title="Elihu Root">Elihu Root</a> of New York. Though Roosevelt won the backing of Treasury Secretary <a href="/wiki/William_Gibbs_McAdoo" title="William Gibbs McAdoo">William Gibbs McAdoo</a> and Governor <a href="/wiki/Martin_H._Glynn" title="Martin H. Glynn">Martin H. Glynn</a>, he faced a formidable opponent in the Tammany-backed <a href="/wiki/James_W._Gerard" title="James W. Gerard">James W. Gerard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007122–123_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007122–123-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He also lacked Wilson's backing, as Wilson needed Tammany's forces to help marshal his legislation and secure his 1916 re-election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195656_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195656-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt was soundly defeated in the Democratic primary by Gerard, who in turn lost the general election to Republican <a href="/wiki/James_Wolcott_Wadsworth_Jr." title="James Wolcott Wadsworth Jr.">James Wolcott Wadsworth Jr.</a> Roosevelt learned a valuable lesson, that federal patronage alone, without White House support, could not defeat a strong local organization.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195657,_60_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195657,_60-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> After the election, Roosevelt and the boss of the Tammany Hall machine, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Francis_Murphy" title="Charles Francis Murphy">Charles Francis Murphy</a>, sought an accommodation with one another and became political allies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007125_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007125-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following his defeat in the Senate primary, Roosevelt refocused on the Navy Department.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007125–126_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007125–126-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> broke out in July 1914, with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> of <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> seeking to defeat the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Powers</a> of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a>. Though he remained publicly supportive of Wilson, Roosevelt sympathized with the <a href="/wiki/Preparedness_Movement" title="Preparedness Movement">Preparedness Movement</a>, whose leaders strongly favored the Allied Powers and called for a military build-up.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201759–61_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201759–61-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The Wilson administration initiated an expansion of the Navy after the <a href="/wiki/Sinking_of_the_RMS_Lusitania" title="Sinking of the RMS Lusitania">sinking of the RMS Lusitania</a> by a German <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a>, and Roosevelt helped establish the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy_Reserve" title="United States Navy Reserve">United States Navy Reserve</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_National_Defense" title="Council of National Defense">Council of National Defense</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007130–132_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007130–132-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In April 1917, after Germany declared it would engage in <a href="/wiki/Unrestricted_submarine_warfare" title="Unrestricted submarine warfare">unrestricted submarine warfare</a> and attacked several U.S. ships, Wilson asked Congress for a declaration of war. Congress approved the <a href="/wiki/United_States_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_(1917)" title="United States declaration of war on Germany (1917)">declaration of war on Germany</a> on April 6.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201762–63_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201762–63-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt requested that he be allowed to serve as a naval officer, but Wilson insisted that he continue to serve as Assistant Secretary of the Navy. For the next year, Roosevelt remained in Washington to coordinate the mobilization, supply, and deployment of naval vessels and personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201765–66_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201765–66-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In the first six months after the U.S. entered the war, the Navy expanded fourfold.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007139–140_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007139–140-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In the summer of 1918, Roosevelt traveled to Europe to inspect naval installations and meet with French and British officials. In September, he returned to the United States on board the <a href="/wiki/SS_Leviathan" title="SS Leviathan">USS <i>Leviathan</i></a>, a large troop carrier. On the 11-day voyage, the <a href="/wiki/1918_flu_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="1918 flu pandemic">pandemic influenza</a> virus struck and killed many on board. Roosevelt became very ill with influenza and a complicating pneumonia, but he recovered by the time the ship landed in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201767–68_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201767–68-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldmanGoldman201715_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldmanGoldman201715-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> After Germany signed an <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_11_November_1918" title="Armistice of 11 November 1918">armistice</a> in November 1918, surrendering and ending the fighting, Daniels and Roosevelt supervised the demobilization of the Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007171–172_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007171–172-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Against the advice of older officers such as Admiral <a href="/wiki/William_S._Benson" title="William S. Benson">William Benson</a>—who claimed he could not "conceive of any use the fleet will ever have for aviation"—Roosevelt personally ordered the preservation of the Navy's <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Aeronautics#Origins:_1920s_and_1930s" title="Bureau of Aeronautics">Aviation Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnderwood199111_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnderwood199111-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> With the Wilson administration coming to an end, Roosevelt began planning for his next run for office. Roosevelt and his associates approached <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a> about running for the 1920 Democratic presidential nomination, with Roosevelt as his running mate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007176–177_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007176–177-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Campaign_for_Vice_President_.281920.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_for_Vice_President_(1920)">Campaign for Vice President (1920)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton,_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton%2C_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg/220px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton%2C_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton%2C_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg/330px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton%2C_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton%2C_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg/440px-Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton%2C_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2833" data-file-height="1845" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franklin_D._Roosevelt_and_James_Cox_in_Dayton,_Ohio_-_NARA_-_197236.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cox and Roosevelt in Ohio, 1920</div></div></div>
<p>Roosevelt's plan to convince Hoover to run for the Democratic nomination fell through after Hoover publicly declared himself to be a Republican, but Roosevelt nonetheless decided to seek the 1920 <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">vice presidential</a> nomination. After Governor <a href="/wiki/James_M._Cox" title="James M. Cox">James M. Cox</a> of Ohio won the party's presidential nomination at the <a href="/wiki/1920_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1920 Democratic National Convention">1920 Democratic National Convention</a>, he chose Roosevelt as his running mate, and the party formally nominated Roosevelt by <a href="/wiki/Acclamation" title="Acclamation">acclamation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007177–181_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007177–181-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Although his nomination surprised most people, Roosevelt <a href="/wiki/Balanced_the_ticket" class="mw-redirect" title="Balanced the ticket">balanced the ticket</a> as a moderate, a Wilsonian, and a <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">prohibitionist</a> with a famous name.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195673_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195673-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunther1950215–16_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunther1950215–16-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt had just turned 38, four years younger than Theodore had been when he received the same nomination from his party. Roosevelt resigned as Assistant Secretary of the Navy after the Democratic convention and campaigned across the nation for the Cox–Roosevelt ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007181_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007181-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1920.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/ElectoralCollege1920.svg/280px-ElectoralCollege1920.svg.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/ElectoralCollege1920.svg/420px-ElectoralCollege1920.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/ElectoralCollege1920.svg/560px-ElectoralCollege1920.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1920.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1920 electoral vote results</div></div></div>
<p>During the campaign, Cox and Roosevelt defended the Wilson administration and the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, both of which were unpopular in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007181–182_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007181–182-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt personally supported U.S. membership in the League of Nations, but, unlike Wilson, he favored compromising with Senator <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cabot_Lodge" title="Henry Cabot Lodge">Henry Cabot Lodge</a> and other "Reservationists."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007175–176_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007175–176-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The Cox–Roosevelt ticket was defeated by Republicans <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Harding" title="Warren G. Harding">Warren G. Harding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Coolidge" title="Calvin Coolidge">Calvin Coolidge</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1920_United_States_presidential_election" title="1920 United States presidential election">presidential election</a> by a wide margin, and the Republican ticket carried every state outside of the South.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns195674_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns195674-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt accepted the loss without issue and later reflected that the relationships and good will that he built in the 1920 campaign proved to be a major asset in his 1932 campaign. The 1920 election also saw the first public participation of Eleanor Roosevelt who, with the support of <a href="/wiki/Louis_Howe" title="Louis Howe">Louis Howe</a>, established herself as a valuable political ally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007182–183_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007182–183-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Paralytic_illness_and_political_comeback_.281921.E2.80.931928.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paralytic_illness_and_political_comeback_(1921–1928)">Paralytic illness and political comeback (1921–1928)</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Paralytic_illness_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Paralytic illness of Franklin D. Roosevelt">Paralytic illness of Franklin D. Roosevelt</a></div>
<p>After the election, Roosevelt returned to New York City, where he practiced law and served as a vice president of the <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_and_Deposit_Company" title="Fidelity and Deposit Company">Fidelity and Deposit Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007184–185_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007184–185-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He also sought to build support for a political comeback in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_elections,_1922" class="mw-redirect" title="United States elections, 1922">1922 elections</a>, but his career was derailed by illness.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007184–185_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007184–185-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> While the Roosevelts were vacationing at Campobello Island in August 1921, he fell ill. His main symptoms were fever; symmetric, ascending paralysis; facial paralysis; bowel and bladder dysfunction; numbness and hyperesthesia; and a descending pattern of recovery. Roosevelt was left permanently paralyzed from the waist down. He was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" class="mw-redirect" title="Poliomyelitis">poliomyelitis</a> at the time, but his symptoms are more consistent with <a href="/wiki/Guillain%E2%80%93Barr%C3%A9_syndrome" title="Guillain–Barré syndrome">Guillain–Barré syndrome</a> – an autoimmune neuropathy which Roosevelt's doctors failed to consider as a diagnostic possibility.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldmanGoldman2017108–147_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldmanGoldman2017108–147-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg/220px-Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg/330px-Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg/440px-Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg 2x" data-file-width="463" data-file-height="566" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roosevelt_in_a_wheelchair.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rare photograph of Roosevelt in a wheelchair, with <a href="/wiki/Fala_(dog)" title="Fala (dog)">Fala</a> and Ruthie Bie, the daughter of caretakers at his Hyde Park estate. Photo taken by his cousin <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Suckley" title="Margaret Suckley">Margaret Suckley</a> (February 1941).</div></div></div>
<p>Though his mother favored his retirement from public life, Roosevelt, his wife, and Roosevelt's close friend and adviser, Louis Howe, were all determined that Roosevelt continue his political career.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007195–196_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007195–196-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt convinced many people that he was improving, which he believed to be essential prior to running for public office again.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERowley2010125_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowley2010125-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> He laboriously taught himself to walk short distances while wearing iron braces on his hips and legs by swiveling his torso, supporting himself with a cane.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERowley2010120_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowley2010120-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt was careful never to be seen using his wheelchair in public, and great care was taken to prevent any portrayal in the press that would highlight his disability.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWardBurns2014332_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWardBurns2014332-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> However, his disability was well known before and during his presidency and became a major part of his image. He usually appeared in public standing upright, supported on one side by an aide or one of his sons.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007220_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007220-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in 1925, Roosevelt spent most of his time in the Southern United States, at first on his houseboat, the <i>Larooco</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007213–214_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007213–214-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Intrigued by the potential benefits of <a href="/wiki/Hydrotherapy" title="Hydrotherapy">hydrotherapy</a>, he established <a href="/wiki/Warm_Springs_Historic_District" title="Warm Springs Historic District">a rehabilitation center</a> at <a href="/wiki/Warm_Springs,_Georgia" title="Warm Springs, Georgia">Warm Springs, Georgia</a>, in 1926. To create the rehabilitation center, Roosevelt assembled a staff of physical therapists and used most of his inheritance to purchase the Merriweather Inn. In 1938, Roosevelt founded the <a href="/wiki/National_Foundation_for_Infantile_Paralysis" class="mw-redirect" title="National Foundation for Infantile Paralysis">National Foundation for Infantile Paralysis</a>, leading to the development of polio vaccines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007215–219_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007215–219-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Roosevelt maintained contacts with the Democratic Party during the 1920s, and he remained active in New York politics while also establishing contacts in the South, particularly in Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007255–256_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007255–256-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt issued an open letter endorsing <a href="/wiki/Al_Smith" title="Al Smith">Al Smith</a>'s successful campaign in New York's 1922 gubernatorial election, which both aided Smith and showed Roosevelt's continuing relevance as a political figure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201787–88_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201787–88-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt and Smith came from different backgrounds and never fully trusted one another, but Roosevelt supported Smith's progressive policies, while Smith was happy to have the backing of the prominent and well-respected Roosevelt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek201787–96_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek201787–96-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt gave presidential nominating speeches for Smith at the 1924 and 1928 Democratic National Conventions; the speech at the 1924 convention marked a return to public life following his illness and convalescence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan1985267,_269–72,_286–87_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan1985267,_269–72,_286–87-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Democrats were badly divided between an urban wing, led by Smith, and a conservative, rural wing, led by <a href="/wiki/William_Gibbs_McAdoo" title="William Gibbs McAdoo">William Gibbs McAdoo</a>, and the party suffered a landslide defeat in the <a href="/wiki/1924_United_States_presidential_election" title="1924 United States presidential election">1924 presidential election</a>. Like many others throughout the United States, Roosevelt did not abstain from alcohol during the Prohibition era, but publicly he sought to find a compromise on Prohibition acceptable to both wings of the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlack2005160–167_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlack2005160–167-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1925, Smith appointed Roosevelt to the <a href="/wiki/Taconic_State_Park" title="Taconic State Park">Taconic State Park</a> Commission, and his fellow commissioners chose him as chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In this role, he came into conflict with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Moses" title="Robert Moses">Robert Moses</a>, a Smith protégé,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> who was the primary force behind the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_State_Park_Commission" title="Long Island State Park Commission">Long Island State Park Commission</a> and the New York State Council of Parks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt accused Moses of using the name recognition of prominent individuals including Roosevelt to win political support for state parks, but then diverting funds to the ones Moses favored on Long Island, while Moses worked to block the appointment of Howe to a salaried position as the Taconic commission's secretary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaro1974289–291-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Roosevelt served on the commission until the end of 1928,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEF._Roosevelt,_E._Roosevelt21_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEF._Roosevelt,_E._Roosevelt21-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> and his contentious relationship with Moses continued as their careers progressed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2007231_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2007231-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Governor_of_New_York_.281929.E2.80.931932.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Governor_of_New_York_(1929–1932)">Governor of New York (1929–1932)</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Governorship_of_Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Governorship of Franklin D. Roosevelt">Governorship of Franklin D. Roosevelt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg/220px-Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="321" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg/330px-Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg/440px-Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg 2x" data-file-width="446" data-file-height="650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Governor_Roosevelt_and_Al_Smith.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gov. Roosevelt with his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Al_Smith" title="Al Smith">Al Smith</a>, 1930</div></div></div>
